# Lisbon Lemon Container Guide — Master Claim Table

**Purpose:** Single source of truth for the guide. Every quantitative target or decision
rule in `lisbon_lemon_guide.md` must trace to a Claim ID here, which traces to a study
note in `..\lisbon-lemon-studies\`. Built by fan-out extraction over all 165 study notes.

**Evidence Strength:** Strong = university extension / govt ag / peer-reviewed / direct
product label · Moderate = commercial or nursery production guide, or repeated across
credible sources · Weak = consumer horticulture or indirect inference · Extrapolated =
container-crop science or citrus-general, not Lisbon-specific.

**Categories (25):** 1 Variety traits · 2 Rootstock/dwarfing · 3 Container size ·
4 Media physical properties · 5 Drainage/perched water · 6 pH targets · 7 EC/salinity ·
8 Nitrogen · 9 Potassium · 10 Ca/Mg · 11 Micronutrients · 12 Fertilizer timing ·
13 Irrigation timing · 14 Leaching/salt mgmt · 15 Transplanting · 16 Pruning ·
17 Staking/support · 18 Flowering/pollination · 19 Fruit maturity/harvest · 20 Pests ·
21 Diseases · 22 Physiological disorders · 23 Heat/wind/cold protection ·
24 Container-specific risks · 25 Common grower errors.

**Total claims:** see count at end. IDs are grouped A–E by extraction batch (no semantic meaning).

## Conflicts & Reconciliations

These tensions surfaced across sources. The guide should follow the **Resolution** column
and cite both underlying claims where relevant.

| # | Tension | Sources | Resolution for a 19"×14" west-facing Brentwood pot |
|---|---------|---------|-----------------------------------------------------|
| 1 | Open the canopy interior for light/sugar **vs** don't thin (dense canopy prevents sunburn) | IFAS selective-pruning vs UC SLO container pruning | Light, **selective** interior thinning only; never hard-thin an exposed west pot; whitewash any newly exposed bark. Favor sunburn protection over maximal light. |
| 2 | Water ~every 3 days (coastal) **vs** ~daily (hot west-facing pot) | UC SLO / UC MG vs heat-stress + container drying notes | Frequency is **weather- and exposure-driven, not fixed** — water to a leaching fraction when the pot tests dry by weight/probe; expect near-daily in heat waves, every 2–3 days in cool marine spells. |
| 3 | Shade cloth 30–50% **vs** flat 50% | Citrus Industry (Tier 1/3) vs consumer sources (Tier 5) | Use **30–50%**, leaning 50% on the west exposure when air temp >95–100°F; trust the extension range over the consumer flat figure. |
| 4 | Repot/root-prune every 2–3 yr **vs** 3–5 yr | UC MG / Simply Trees vs Clemson | Interval scales with pot size and vigor; for a **19" pot on dwarfing rootstock, ~2–3 yr** root-prune + media refresh. |
| 5 | Salt-tolerant rootstocks (Alemow/Volkamer) are the **least** size-controlling; size-controlling trifoliates are the **most** salt-sensitive | UCR + Scientia Hort. + Citrus Australia | You generally can't get both. For a small pot **prioritize dwarfing (Flying Dragon / C-35)** and manage salt by leaching + good water, not by rootstock. |
| 6 | Light **pot** color cools the root zone, but a white **wall** bounces radiant heat onto the canopy | container-color study vs balcony radiant-heat note | Use a **light-colored pot**, but avoid a highly reflective wall directly behind the canopy; shade cloth handles reflected load. |
| 7 | pH target 5.5–6.5 (Lisbon care) **vs** ~6.0–7.0 (broader citrus) | Lisbon care guide vs TN State / Purdue | Target **~6.0–6.5**; at the high end rely on Fe-EDDHA chelate selection (A020/SS423) rather than fighting pH. |
| 8 | Carrizo/Troyer citrange as rootstock | Carrizo note (Tier 1) | **Documented incompatibility with Eureka-type lemons** + salt/high-pH sensitivity → do NOT use for Lisbon; choose Flying Dragon or C-35. |
| 9 | Mal secco as a disease threat | Lisbon disease-susceptibility note | **Not present in California** — exclude as a local threat; list only for completeness/biosecurity. |
| 10 | Greasy spot: water "late in day" **vs** water in morning for fast leaf-drying | UC IPM greasy-spot note (internal ambiguity) | **Water in the morning** so the canopy dries fast (greasy-spot control); the "late in day" phrasing is superseded. |
| 11 | Biochar optimum 20% (measured) **vs** 10–15% cap (alkaline-water pH risk) | biochar rootstock-substrate study | Cap at **10–15%** of mix volume given hard alkaline LA tap water; preserve the measured 20% figure as the un-constrained optimum. |
| 12 | Field micronutrient/N rates (lb/acre, lb/tree) | IFAS SS423 / UA fertilization chart | **Do not transfer** field rates to a pot; use labeled foliar/CRF products and downscale — flagged on every field-rate claim. |

## Provenance
- 693 claims extracted from 165 study notes (batches A–E, ~33 notes each).
- Heaviest evidence: root-zone thermal management, substrate physical properties/aeration,
  irrigation/leaching/salinity, rootstock/dwarfing, pruning, and UC IPM pest/disease.
- Thinnest evidence: genuinely **Lisbon-specific** container numbers (most are extrapolated
  from citrus-general or container-crop science) — see Evidence Gaps in `_source_catalog.md`.
